  471. Earlier, I left a one-star review for this product, as the bottle I got smelled AWFUL. I mean, just horrific. As soon as I left the review, the seller contacted me, refunded my money and sent me a new bottle to try and review.<br /><br />I've actually spent several days now trying to figure out how I feel about it. The first thing that's clear to me is that previously, I did indeed get a batch that was somehow spoiled. The fresh bottle they sent me did not smell like the first one.<br /><br />It's a very uniquely scented rose water, and it's VERY VERY STRONG. It lingers wherever it goes for hours. When I tossed a used cotton pad into the bathroom bin, it made the entire bathroom smell that way for the entire day before finally fading.<br /><br />However, within that unique smell is some scent I can't identify that keeps putting me off. I've seriously been taking random sniffs for days and thinking as hard as possible to try to figure out what this reminds me of that I just can't remember. It's not really good, actually, but it's also not horrible. But most of all, whatever it is, it's NOT ROSES. I have several other brands of rose waters that I cycle through using, and overall, this rose water does not smell ANYTHING like those.<br /><br />The thing is, whatever it smells like is a very familiar scent, but I still can't put my finger on it. I had my husband sniff it and he had to think a while before finally guessing it smelled like cheap perfume. I told him it was rose water, and he frowned and thought for a while longer and said, \\"Maybe over-extracted roses?\\" Since I don't know the process for making rose water, I have no idea how it works and if that's a thing, but it did sort of match in my mind. Like how over-extracted coffee smells bad, you know? It still smells like coffee, but it has some other note in there that makes it sour. So it really does feel like maybe it's some seriously aggressive attempt to make this smell as powerful as possible.<br /><br />That said, scents are one of those things that are very personal and tastes vary widely. I see there are a ton of reviews that enthuse about the good smell of this product. I am not sure why no one else is smelling what I am. I know that I'm not nose-deaf, and in fact am one of those \\"super smeller\\" people who have a heightened sense of smell and taste and can pick out subtle notes in a scent. And I know I know what roses smell like, and as I stated before I have several different brands of rose water I use, and they all smell like roses and nothing but roses. So this, I don't know what's happening here. I doubt that I got *yet another* spoiled bottle, but it's still just not a product I would immediately identify as rose water if someone used it for a blind smell-test.<br /><br />Edit: Okay, wow, I went to go take a photo of the rose water so I could show the nice new label and that the rose water is perfectly clear, and I decided (against my better judgement) to taste it. That's when I realized what it was that it smelled like. Soap. It doesn't taste BAD, like, omg I have to spit this out bad, but it has a very distinct taste of soap. What it smells like is rose soap. It has a sort of artificial scent to it, which is why it was so difficult for me to identify. I was not expecting \\"soap\\" to be the scent I was missing.<br /><br />I don't know about you all, but I have tasted culinary grade rose water, and I have eaten turkish delight (one of the most traditional, common flavors is rose, and uses rosewater to impart that taste) and this is just not at all your standard rose water. It just is not it. When I use my other brands of rose water my husband sometimes remarks that I smell like turkish delight. As I mentioned earlier, when I presented him with this bottle, his first guess was *not* rose water.<br /><br />So, really, I don't know what's going on with this rose water, or why it's so extraordinarily strong, why it lingers much (MUCH) longer than other rose waters, or why it has that extra, somewhat-artificial 'soap' scent to it, but I know it's not for me. Clearly, as you can see by other reviews, others find the scent delightful and love the product. I could not even use it on my face because the smell was too strong for me to actually keep on my skin. I put it on my wrist for a time and had no particular skin reaction, but I just couldn't say how it would work as a facial toner because I could never get past the smell.<br /><br />In summary, I suppose I could say this much - try it, if you're trying out rose waters, and rest assured that the seller absolutely DOES mean what it says when it offers a money-back guarantee.
